       1                 :            : // *****************************************************************************
       2                 :            : /*!
       3                 :            :   \file      src/Control/Keywords.hpp
       4                 :            :   \copyright 2012-2015 J. Bakosi,
       5                 :            :              2016-2018 Los Alamos National Security, LLC.,
       6                 :            :              2019-2020 Triad National Security, LLC.
       7                 :            :              All rights reserved. See the LICENSE file for details.
       8                 :            :   \brief     Definition of all keywords
       9                 :            :   \details   This file contains the definition of all keywords, including those
      10                 :            :     of command-line argument parsers as well as input, i.e., control, file
      11                 :            :     parsers. All keywords are shared among all parsers of all executables.
      12                 :            : 
      13                 :            :     All keywords are case-sensitive.
      14                 :            : 
      15                 :            :     The information contained in this file is used to build data structures for
      16                 :            :     on-screen help on the command-line arguments and control file keywords,
      17                 :            :     available via the --help, --helpctr, and --helpkw command-line arguments.
      18                 :            : 
      19                 :            :     A note on design: Defining structs that have static member functions
      20                 :            :     returning a std::string is a way of storing C++-style strings at
      21                 :            :     compile-time (which is not possible in a straightforward manner at this
      22                 :            :     time). This could also be done with C-style const char* as well. The
      23                 :            :     '*_info' structs store these strings, which then is used to specialize the
      24                 :            :     _kw::keyword_ template, defined in Control/Keyword.hpp. Specializing the
      25                 :            :     _keyword_ template also requires a specification of the precise string of
      26                 :            :     characters that make up a keyword eventually matched by the parsers. Since
      27                 :            :     these are all template arguments, the construction of keywords, their help,
      28                 :            :     as well as all grammars, are entirely assembled at compile-time. Since the
      29                 :            :     '*_info' struct member functions are static, they can be called without
      30                 :            :     instantiating an object and thus available at compile-time.
      31                 :            : 
      32                 :            :     The definition of an '*_info' struct _requires_ at least the name, short,
      33                 :            :     and long descriptions, defined by member functions _name()_,
      34                 :            :     _shortDescription()_, and _longDescription()_, respectively. Everything else
      35                 :            :     is optional. However, when adding a new keyword it is highly recommended to
      36                 :            :     define all of the _optional_ members if they make sense for the given
      37                 :            :     keyword. If an expect value type is also given, that can be hooked up into
      38                 :            :     where it is used.
      39                 :            : 
      40                 :            :     The most general definition of a keyword is as follows:
      41                 :            : 
      42                 :            :     \code{.cpp}
      43                 :            :       // Keyword info definition
      44                 :            :       struct keyword_info {
      45                 :            : 
      46                 :            :         // Required very short name, usually a single word or (for e.g.
      47                 :            :         // policies) a single character. This can be the keyword itself, but
      48                 :            :         // does not have to be. This field is used as an id of the option or
      49                 :            :         // setting.
      50                 :            :         static std::string name() { return "Name"; }
      51                 :            : 
      52                 :            :         // Required short keyword description
      53                 :            :         static std::string shortDescription() { return "Short description"; }
      54                 :            : 
      55                 :            :         // Required detailed keyword description. This returns a string literal,
      56                 :            :         // since this is usually multi-line and it is less work to maintain this
      57                 :            :         // way.
      58                 :            :         static std::string longDescription() { return
      59                 :            :           R"(Longer, possibly multi-line description of the keyword. Example
      60                 :            :           usage of the keyword is welcome here. Don't worry about formatting:
      61                 :            :           when this field is printed, extra spaces will be removed and line
      62                 :            :           breaks will be inserted.)";
      63                 :            :         }
      64                 :            : 
      65                 :            :         // Optional keyword alias. See also kw::Alias and
      66                 :            :         // <tpl_install_dir>/include/pegtl/pegtl/constants.hh for examples
      67                 :            :         // of what can be passed as template arguments (basically single
      68                 :            :         // characters). The one below defines the character 'c' as the alias.
      69                 :            :         // Aliases are single character long. The idea of an alias is to have a
      70                 :            :         // long as well as a short keyword for the same functionality.
      71                 :            :         // Currently, this is only hooked up for command-line arguments and not
      72                 :            :         // for control-file keywords, which is intentional. Command-line
      73                 :            :         // arguments are a lot less than control file keywords and are more
      74                 :            :         // frequently typed by the user. Thus command-line argument aliases are
      75                 :            :         // user-friendly. There are many control file keywords and aliases would
      76                 :            :         // only cause confusion. Defining an alias for a command-line argument
      77                 :            :         // enables the command-line parser to match on '--longer_keyword' as
      78                 :            :         // well as on '-c'. Depending on whether the alias typedef is defined
      79                 :            :         // for a keyword or not, the correct grammar is automatically generated
      80                 :            :         // at compile-time, matching on both the longer keyword as well as on
      81                 :            :         // the alias. Defining an alias for a control file keyword can be done
      82                 :            :         // but has no effect in a control file parser.
      83                 :            :         using alias = Alias< c >;
      84                 :            : 
      85                 :            :         // Optional single-character (policy) code. See also kw::Code and
      86                 :            :         // <tpl_install_dir/include/pegtl/pegtl/constants.hh for examples
      87                 :            :         // of what can be passed as template arguments (basically single
      88                 :            :         // characters). The one below defines the character 'C' as the (policy)
      89                 :            :         // code. This code is used for abbreviating policies used to configure
      90                 :            :         // various orthogonal behaviors of classes using policy-based design.
      91                 :            :         using code = Code< C >;
      92                 :            : 
      93                 :            :         // Optional expected data for the keyword - bundled to struct expect.
      94                 :            :         // This struct is entirely optional within a keyword definition.
      95                 :            :         // However, if it is defined, it must at least define the static member
      96                 :            :         // function description() which returns the description of the type the
      97                 :            :         // keyword expects. It may also optionally define the following fields:
      98                 :            :         //
      99                 :            :         //    - type - defining the expected type
     100                 :            :         //    - lower - lower bound of the expected value
     101                 :            :         //    - upper - upper bound of the expected value
     102                 :            :         //    - choices - valid choices for the expected value
     103                 :            :         //
     104                 :            :         struct expect {
     105                 :            : 
     106                 :            :           // If this struct is defined, required expected type description, max
     107                 :            :           // 10 characters long
     108                 :            :           static std::string description() { return "int"; }
     109                 :            : 
     110                 :            :           // Optional expected type
     111                 :            :           using type = std::streamsize;
     112                 :            : 
     113                 :            :           // Optional expected value lower bound
     114                 :            :           static const type lower = 1;
     115                 :            : 
     116                 :            :           // Optional expected value upper bound
     117                 :            :           static const type upper =
     118                 :            :             std::numeric_limits< tk::real >::digits10 + 1;
     119                 :            : 
     120                 :            :           // Optional expected valid choices description, here giving
     121                 :            :           // information on the expected type and the valid bounds. Note that
     122                 :            :           // this can be any string, but if they exist, it is a good idea give
     123                 :            :           // at least some information on the bounds, as below, since the bounds
     124                 :            :           // are NOT displayed in the help for a keyword. This decision keeps
     125                 :            :           // the bounds specifications generic since they can be any type. As a
     126                 :            :           // result, the help structures, defined in HelpFactory.hpp, are simpler
     127                 :            :           // as they do not have to be parameterized by the type of the bounds,
     128                 :            :           // which greatly simplifies that code.
     129                 :            :           static std::string choices() {
     130                 :            :             return "integer [" + std::to_string(lower) + "..." +
     131                 :            :                    std::to_string(upper) + ']';
     132                 :            :           }
     133                 :            : 
     134                 :            :         };
     135                 :            : 
     136                 :            :       };
     137                 :            : 
     138                 :            :       // Keyword definition, passing the above info struct as the first
     139                 :            :       // template argument, and the rest of the template arguments are the
     140                 :            :       // characters of the keyword to be matched by the parser. Remember: all
     141                 :            :       // keywords are case-sensitive. This one contrived example below defines
     142                 :            :       // keyword 'kw', matching the keyword 'KeYwOrD'.
     143                 :            :       using kw = keyword< keyword_info, K,e,Y,w,O,r,D >;
     144                 :            :     \endcode
     145                 :            :   \see Control/Keyword.hpp
     146                 :            :   \see Control/HelpFactory.hpp
     147                 :            : */
     148                 :            : // *****************************************************************************
     149                 :            : #ifndef Keywords_h
     150                 :            : #define Keywords_h
     151                 :            : 
     152                 :            : #include <limits>
     153                 :            : 
     154                 :            : #include <pegtl/contrib/alphabet.hpp>
     155                 :            : 
     156                 :            : #include "Types.hpp"
     157                 :            : #include "Keyword.hpp"
     158                 :            : #include "QuinoaConfig.hpp"
     159                 :            :

     161                 :            : namespace kw {

     170                 :            :     keyword. The 'title' keyword must be followed by a double-quoted string
     171                 :            :     specifying the analysis title. Example: title "Example problem".

    1482                 :            : struct homdecay_info {
    1483                 :            :   using code = Code< Y >;
    1484                 :            :   static std::string name() { return "homogeneous decay"; }
    1485                 :            :   static std::string shortDescription() { return
    1486                 :            :     "Select homogeneous decay coefficients policy"; }
    1487                 :            :   static std::string longDescription() { return
    1488                 :            :     R"(This keyword is used to select the homogeneous decay coefficients policy.
    1489                 :            :     This policy (or model) is used to constrain a beta stochastic differential
    1490                 :            :     equation so that its variance, <y^2>, always decays and its mean, <R> =
    1491                 :            :     rho2/(1+r<RY>/<R>), where Y = <Y> + y, does not change in time. Note that
    1492                 :            :     R = rho2/(1+rY). This policy is similar to 'montecarlo_homdecay', but
    1493                 :            :     computes the SDE coefficient S in a different but statistically equivalent
    1494                 :            :     way. While 'homdecay' only requires the estimation of statistics, <R>,
    1495                 :            :     <r^2>, and <r^3>, 'montecarlo_homdecay' requires <R^2>, <YR^2>, and
    1496                 :            :     <Y(1-Y)R^3>. A coefficients policy, in general, is used to specify how the
    1497                 :            :     coefficients are set at each time step during time-integration. Example:
    1498                 :            :     "coeff const", which selects constant coefficients policy, which sets
    1499                 :            :     constant coefficients before t = 0 and leaves the coefficients unchanged
    1500                 :            :     during time integration. Note that this option may behave differently
    1501                 :            :     depending on the particular equation or physical model.)"; }

    1517                 :            :     statistically equivalent way. While 'homdecay' only requires the estimation

    2984                 :            :     specify the configuration of a system of number-fraction beta SDEs, a system
    2985                 :            :     of stochastic differential equations (SDEs), in which, in addition to the
    2986                 :            :     dependent variable, computed with linear drift and quadratic diagonal
    2987                 :            :     diffusion (whose invariant is joint beta), two additional variables are
    2988                 :            :     computed. In other words, this is a beta SDE but there are two additional
    2989                 :            :     stochastic variables computed based on the beta SDE. If X is governed by the
    2990                 :            :     beta SDE, then the number-fraction beta SDE additionally governs rho(X) and
    2991                 :            :     V(X), where both rho and V are random variables, computed by rho(X) = rho2
    2992                 :            :     ( 1 - r' X ), and V(X) = 1 / [ rho2 ( 1 - r'X ) ]. For more details on the
    2993                 :            :     beta SDE, see https://doi.org/10.1080/14685248.2010.510843 and
    2994                 :            :     src/DiffEq/Beta/Beta.hpp. Keywords allowed in a numfracbeta ... end block: )"
    2995                 :            :     + std::string("\'")
    2996                 :            :     + depvar::string()+ "\', \'"
    2997                 :            :     + ncomp::string() + "\', \'"
    2998                 :            :     + rng::string() + "\', \'"
    2999                 :            :     + init::string() + "\', \'"

    3047                 :            : struct mixnumfracbeta_info {
    3048                 :            :   static std::string name() { return "Mix number-fraction beta"; }
    3049                 :            :   static std::string shortDescription() { return
    3050                 :            :     "Introduce the mixnumfracbeta SDE input block"; }
    3051                 :            :   static std::string longDescription() { return
    3052                 :            :     R"(This keyword is used to introduce a mixnumfracbeta ... end block, used
    3053                 :            :     to specify the configuration of a system of mix number-fraction beta SDEs, a
    3054                 :            :     system of stochastic differential equations (SDEs), whose solution is the
    3055                 :            :     joint beta distribution and in which the usual beta SDE parameters b and
    3056                 :            :     kappa are specified via functions that constrain the beta SDE to be
    3057                 :            :     consistent with the turbulent mixing process. The mix number-fraction beta
    3058                 :            :     SDE is similar to the number-fraction beta SDE, only the process is made
    3059                 :            :     consistent with the no-mix and fully mixed limits via the specification of
    3060                 :            :     the SDE coefficients b and kappa. As in the number-fraction beta SDE, X is
    3061                 :            :     governed by the beta SDE and two additional stochastic variables are
    3062                 :            :     computed. However, in the mix number-fraction beta SDE the parameters b and
    3063                 :            :     kappa are given by b = Theta * b' and kappa = kappa' * <x^2>, where Theta =
    3064                 :            :     1 - <x^2> / [ <X> ( 1 - <X> ], the fluctuation about the mean, <X>, is
    3065                 :            :     defined as usual: x = X - <X>, and b' and kappa' are user-specified
    3066                 :            :     constants. Similar to the number-fraction beta SDE, there two additional
    3067                 :            :     random variables computed besides, X, and they are rho(X) and V(X). For more
    3068                 :            :     detail on the number-fraction beta SDE, see the help on keyword
    3069                 :            :     'numfracbeta'. For more details on the beta SDE, see
    3070                 :            :     https://doi.org/10.1080/14685248.2010.510843 and src/DiffEq/Beta/Beta.h.
    3071                 :            :     Keywords allowed in a mixnumfracbeta ... end block: )"
    3072                 :            :     + std::string("\'")
    3073                 :            :     + depvar::string()+ "\', \'"
    3074                 :            :     + ncomp::string() + "\', \'"
    3075                 :            :     + rng::string() + "\', \'"
    3076                 :            :     + init::string() + "\', \'"
    3077                 :            :     + coeff::string() + "\', \'"
    3078                 :            :     + sde_bprime::string() + "\', \'"
    3079                 :            :     + sde_S::string() + "\', \'"
    3080                 :            :     + sde_kappaprime::string() + "\', \'"
    3081                 :            :     + sde_rho2::string() + "\', \'"
    3082                 :            :     + sde_rcomma::string() + "\'. "
    3083                 :            :     + R"(For an example mixnumfracbeta ... end block, see
    3084                 :            :       doc/html/walker_example_mixnumfracbeta.html.)";
    3085                 :            :   }

    3358                 :            : struct mixmassfracbeta_info {
    3359                 :            :   static std::string name() { return "Mix mass-fraction beta"; }
    3360                 :            :   static std::string shortDescription() { return
    3361                 :            :     "Introduce the mixmassfracbeta SDE input block"; }
    3362                 :            :   static std::string longDescription() { return
    3363                 :            :     R"(This keyword is used in multiple ways: (1) To introduce a mixmassfracbeta
    3364                 :            :     ... end block, used to specify the configuration of a system of mix
    3365                 :            :     mass-fraction beta SDEs, a system of stochastic differential equations
    3366                 :            :     (SDEs), whose solution is the joint beta distribution and in which the usual
    3367                 :            :     beta SDE parameters b and kappa are specified via functions that constrain
    3368                 :            :     the beta SDE to be consistent with the turbulent mixing process. The mix
    3369                 :            :     mass-fraction beta SDE is similar to the mass-fraction beta SDE, only the
    3370                 :            :     process is made consistent with the no-mix and fully mixed limits via the
    3371                 :            :     specification of the SDE coefficients b and kappa. As in the mass-fraction
    3372                 :            :     beta SDE, Y is governed by the beta SDE and two additional stochastic
    3373                 :            :     variables are computed. However, in the mix mass-fraction beta SDE the
    3374                 :            :     parameters b and kappa are given by b = Theta * b' and kappa = kappa' *
    3375                 :            :     <y^2>, where Theta = 1 - <y^2> / [ <Y> ( 1 - <Y> ], the fluctuation about
    3376                 :            :     the mean, <Y>, is defined as usual: y = Y - <Y>, and b' and kappa' are
    3377                 :            :     user-specified constants. Similar to the mass-fraction beta SDE, there two
    3378                 :            :     additional random variables computed besides, Y, and they are rho(Y) and
    3379                 :            :     V(Y). For more detail on the mass-fraction beta SDE, see the help on keyword
    3380                 :            :     'massfracbeta'. For more details on the beta SDE, see
    3381                 :            :     https://doi.org/10.1080/14685248.2010.510843 and src/DiffEq/Beta/Beta.hpp.
    3382                 :            :     Keywords allowed in a mixmassfracbeta ... end block: )"
    3383                 :            :     + std::string("\'")
    3384                 :            :     + depvar::string()+ "\', \'"
    3385                 :            :     + ncomp::string() + "\', \'"
    3386                 :            :     + rng::string() + "\', \'"
    3387                 :            :     + init::string() + "\', \'"
    3388                 :            :     + coeff::string() + "\', \'"
    3389                 :            :     + sde_bprime::string() + "\', \'"
    3390                 :            :     + sde_S::string() + "\', \'"
    3391                 :            :     + sde_kappaprime::string() + "\', \'"
    3392                 :            :     + sde_rho2::string() + "\', \'"
    3393                 :            :     + hydrotimescales::string() + "\', \'"
    3394                 :            :     + hydroproductions::string() + "\', \'"
    3395                 :            :     + "velocity" + "\', \'"
    3396                 :            :     + "dissipation" + "\', \'"

    3970                 :            :     virtualization or over-decomposition. Independent of the value of
    3971                 :            :     virtualization the work is approximately evenly distributed among the
    3972                 :            :     available processing elements. For zero virtualization (no
    3973                 :            :     over-decomposition), the work is simply decomposed into
    3974                 :            :     total_work/numPEs, which yields the smallest number of Charm++ chares and
    3975                 :            :     the largest chunks of work units. The other extreme is unity
    3976                 :            :     virtualization, which decomposes the total work into the smallest size
    3977                 :            :     work units possible, yielding the largest number of Charm++ chares.

    5582                 :            :     (i.e., earlier in the input file) selected dependent variables can be
    5583                 :            :     configured as refinement variables. Dependent variables are required to be
    5584                 :            :     defined in all equation system configuration blocks, e.g., transport ...
    5585                 :            :     end, by using the 'depvar' keyword. Example: transport depvar c end amr
    5586                 :            :     refvar c end end. Selecting a particular scalar component in a system is
    5587                 :            :     done by appending the equation number to the refvar: Example: transport
    5588                 :            :     depvar q ncomp 3 end amr refvar q1 q2 end end, which configures two
    5589                 :            :     refinement variables: the first and third scalar component of the previously
    5590                 :            :     configured transport equation system.)"; }

    5592                 :            :     static std::string description() { return "strings"; }
    5593                 :            :   };
